After I completed for you, O Son, this book which is the last of medical knowledge with its supplement, and I reached its end through its explanations and clarifications, it seemed fitting to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of practice, that is surgery, by hand.
Since manual operation has been prostrated in our region and time, and has altogether been deprived until its knowledge may have perished, and its trace been cut off, and nothing remains of it but small descriptions in ancient books which were altered by hands, and error and hesitation occurred to them until their intentions were closed, and its way was lengthened, it seemed fitting to me to revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise therein according to the way of explanation, clarification, and abbreviation: and that I may come with forms of instruments for cautery, and other tools of operation, through addition of clarifications and expediting what is necessary.
The reason why no good artisan of it with his own hand is found in our time is because the art of medicine is long, and its author must exercise himself beforehand therein in the science of anatomy which Galen narrated until he knows the joints of members, their forms, their connection and separation, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, sinews, their number and course, and pulsating veins and quiet ones, and their outlets.
And because of this Hippocrates said that 'a name with a name is much, but with work it is little, especially in the art of hand.'
But we have already spoken about him at the beginning of this book.
Since whoever is not knowing what we have said about anatomy will certainly fall into error whereby people are killed, as I have seen many of those who claim to be formed in this knowledge and boast about it without knowledge and experience.
That is because I saw a foolish physician cut open an abscess on the neck of a woman and sever certain arteries in her neck: wherefore blood flowed from the woman until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to remove a stone from a man who had grown old with it, and the stone was large. He went forth therefore unto him, and drew out the stone together with part of the bladder. Wherefore the man died on the third day.
But I myself had already been called unto to remove it, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the sick man, he would die.
And I saw another physician who received payment from a certain Duke of our land because of his medicine: and it happened that there was a fracture in the leg of a black eunuch who was with him near the heel. And the physician hastened with his ignorance, and bound the fracture over the wound with bandages and strong ligatures without allowing the wound to breathe.
Then he dismissed him according to his desire. Afterwards he let him go for some days and ordered him not to loose the bandage: and so it remained until his leg and foot became gangrenous and were destroyed.
I was therefore called unto him, and hastened to loose the bandage: and quietness followed, and he escaped from his pains.
However, the gangrene had already become confirmed in the member, and I could not check it.
So therefore the corruption spread throughout the member until he died.
And I saw another physician who punctured a cancerous abscess, and it became ulcerated afterwards, until its wickedness grew great with its owner.
This is because when an abscess is pure from black bile humor, then it should not be pierced with iron at all unless it is on a member that can tolerate it being completely cut off.
And therefore, O Son, it is necessary for you to know that an operation with the hand is divided into two divisions: namely, an operation associated with health, and an operation with which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have already indicated in every place of this book where an operation comes that causes fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of this and avoid it: so that fools may not find a way to speak about it and bring dishonor upon it.
Therefore take measure with care and protection, and your patients with ease and steadfastness. Use the better path leading by God's grace to health and praiseworthy success. Leave behind terrible illnesses that are difficult to cure, and free yourselves from that which causes you fear, lest doubt should enter upon your faith and comfort.
For it is more remaining for your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally for your profit.
For Galen has already said in certain of his admonitions. Do not treat an illness badly, lest you be called bad physicians.
Now however, I have divided this Treatise into three chapters:
Chapter one.
Concerning the cautery with fire and the cautery with sharp medicine, arranged and ordered from head to foot, and forms of instruments and implements of the cautery: and all that is necessary for the operation.
Chapter two.
Concerning section and perforation, bloodletting and wounds, and extraction of arrows, and similar things: and all arranged and ordered with forms of instruments.
Chapter Three.
Concerning restoration and reduction, and treatment of dislocations, and similar things: all arranged and ordered from head to foot with forms of instruments.
But before I mention the operation concerning it, it is necessary that I should speak of the benefits and harms of it, and in which constitution it should be exhibited.
I say therefore that the discourse concerning the benefit and harm of cautery is a long and subtle science, and a hidden secret.
Many wise men have spoken about it and they disagreed; but for me, a few words will suffice, lest I prolong (the discussion).
I say therefore that cautery is beneficial for every constitution, whether it has matter or not; except for two constitutions, namely a hot constitution without matter and a dry constitution without matter.
But concerning the hot and dry constitution with matter, they disagreed. Some said that cautery is beneficial for it. And others said the opposite of that, namely that cautery is not suitable for an illness that arises from heat and dryness: because the nature of fire is heat, and it is unsuitable to heal an illness that is hot and dry with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite of that said: by cautery there is benefit for every hot and dry illness that occurs in human bodies; because when you compare the body of a man and its moistures to the constitution of fire, you find the body of a man cold.
I myself say through his words: for it has been proven true to me many times through experience.
But nevertheless it is not fitting that anyone should approach this matter except one who has already been proven and trained in the final chapter of Cautery Practice, and has known the diversity of human constitutions, and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, accidents, and duration.
But as for other constitutions, there is no fear over them. And especially in cold and moist illnesses. For all doctors have agreed on these matters, and they do not disagree about using cautery to benefit them.
And know, sons, that the secret of healing by cautery with fire and its good quality is such that it burns only the member being cauterized, and does not harm any other connected member unless there is a slight injury.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that which is distant from members, and perhaps causes difficult-to-heal illnesses to occur in a member, and perhaps even kills.
But fire, due to its fineness and good substance, does not do this unless there is an excess.
But we have learned this through experience due to the length of our service and study with this art, and our diligence in searching for the truth of things. And therefore I excuse myself for the length of this discourse.
And if it were not for the fact that this book of mine does not allow me to reveal to you the secret hidden in fire and the quality of its operation on bodies for driving out illnesses, which demonstrates by philosophical proof that it sharpens your minds.
And know, my sons, that they disagree at the time when cautery is to be performed, and they set a better time for the truth.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times: for the harm that occurs because of time is submerged in the benefit that is drawn along with cautery. And especially if cautery is performed because of pains from necessary, strong, and urgent ailments that do not tolerate delay; for it is feared that a greater harm may result from them than the slight harm caused by waiting for the right time.
And do not fall into the error, my sons, which is held only by the common people and foolish physicians, that there is no return to health after an ailment has been cured by cautery; they assert this consequence, but it is not so; for cautery is employed only in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries up the moistures which are the cause of pains.
Nevertheless, cautery exceeds medicine in the swiftness of its cure, and the strength of its operation, and the vehemence of its power; it is possible that an ailment may return at some later time according to the constitution of the patient, and the location and nature of the ailment, and its strength; and what accumulates in his body from superfluities in him, and what reaches it through food and similar causes, unless he becomes ill with one in which cautery is administered.
A subtle ailment in a member with few superfluities and moistures, such as the pain of a toothache, for example, may not return. But this happens rarely.
However, the common belief that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not entirely accurate. People think that there is no cure after cautery.
On the contrary, cautery is not really the last resort of medicine; rather, it is used only when other methods of treatment have failed to bring about a cure.
The ancients said that cautery with gold is better than with iron, and they said this because of the fineness of gold and its exalted nature. They also said that it does not cause pus at the site of the cautery. But this is not absolutely true. For I have already proven that [cautery with gold] does not cause pus in some bodies without other complications.
And indeed cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you use fire cautery with gold, it is not clear how much heat you are applying due to the redness of the gold. Moreover, if you increase the heat, the gold will melt in the fire and become liquefied.
Therefore, the craftsman becomes confused by this. And for that reason, we use cautery with iron more quickly and accurately in our operations.
And I have already arranged this chapter on cautery according to the chapters, and ordered them from head to foot, so that whoever seeks something may find it easily.
Chapter 2.
Here the cautery is useful for the lordship of humidity and coldness above the brain: which two are causes of madness and multitude of flows of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and multitude of sleep, and toothache, and sore throat, and universally all diseases that occur from coldness, such as paralysis, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The method of cauterization is this: you should advise the patient to evacuate first with a cleansing solvent medicine for three nights or four, according to what the strength of the patient requires and their age and habit.
Then instruct him to shave his head with a razor. Then have him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has placed his hands on his chest.
Then place the root of your palm over the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger reaches, mark that spot with a cauter.
Then take the olive-oil cautery: of which this is the shape:
Then place it on the marked spot with descent, as your hand is gradually tightened, and you turn it. Then quickly remove your hand, and examine the spot.
But if you see that now a quantity of alkiel has been released from the bone, or a quantity of zeuherbi, then raise your hand. And if not, repeat the cautery with the same iron or another if it has cooled until you see the bones which I have told you.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water and sprinkle it on the spot, and let him rest for three days.
Next, place upon it butter into which is soaked the mixture, and leave it there until the burn is destroyed. Then treat it with ointment tetrapharmacon until it heals.
They say that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits: therefore it is better and more helpful to keep it open.
And some of them say that the skin should be cauterized up to the bone and held until something of the thickness of the bone is burned.
Then shave what has been burned from the bone, and then treat it.
And others say that one must come with the cautery to the final point until it makes an impression on the bone like a brand or instrument for lettering: and they think that from this place vapors of the head escape, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it until it heals.
But these two methods of cautery seem to me useful only for certain people according to their nature and temperament.
I think it is better to leave it alone with care for its well-being.
For the head is weakened by breaking its natural continuity; as we have seen in other members, especially when it has a weak nature. The first method of cautery seems to me safer and better, and I use it; therefore act with caution.
Chapter Three.
When chronic headache occurs and persists in a patient despite the use of medicines such as hyeres, cochis, caput-purgatives, oils, and emplasters. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the cautery that I have described, and none of those remedies help: then consider. For if the head of the patient is robust by nature and not weak, and a violent chill is found: then cauterize with another cautery beneath it slightly. Then cauterize the horn of the head itself with the cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover as much bone as I have described. And cauterize it with the cautery at the back of the head itself, in the place called 'the vessel': which is where the windpipe is placed, and raise your hand slightly there, without uncovering the bone. For the patient finds great pain in this, different from the pain of all other head cauteries.
And I say that this cautery should be used in its place; and it is necessary that there should be a cautery for burning the horns of the head, and a finer one for burning the back of the head, which is also used for burning the middle of the head.
Chapter IV.
When pain and stiffness occurs in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is cleansed with medicines that purify it, and the rest of the treatment that I have described for the divisions of illnesses is administered, but nothing helps: then cautery is performed on it in two ways: either cauterization with burning acute medicine, or with iron.
The cautery with burning acute medicine is this: take one clove of garlic, peel it, and cut off its ends on both sides. Then incise the painful area in the temple with a wide lancet until there is made beneath the skin a place to hold the garlic.
Then insert it beneath the skin until it is hidden; then bind it with a suitable bandage of lint and leave it for fifteen hours. Then remove the garlic and let the wound remain open for two or three days. Afterwards, apply butter in which a piece of cotton has been immersed until pus forms. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish to do this with certain medicines that burn, which I have written about in the twelfth book on burning medications.
Cautery of it with iron is done in this manner. The form of the cautery used for fire is as follows.
And it is called the 'Claw': because the shape of its head is like that of a nail, with some curvature and a small prominence in the middle.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand steady; you turn the iron gradually with speed, and let the amount that is burned be equal to the thickness of the skin. And raise your hand so that the artery below is not burnt, lest blood flow should occur.
Then bathe the wound with salt water and apply it to the spot; leave it for three days. Then apply butter to the wound. Afterwards treat it with ointment until it heals.
And if you wish, cauterize this half of the head with the second edge of the cautery. Beware of cutting the artery in this case, as it is not proper for an old wound.
Regarding the method of cauterizing in an old head wound.
When treating a head wound with what we have said about previous treatments and the divisions of illnesses, but the treatment does not help and you see that the illness is severe and that cautery with medicine or fire alone is insufficient, then take the cautery with the knife-like edge until it turns white. Then mark the spot of pain with a line whose length is half a fingerbreadth or roughly that amount. Then place your hand once and press it down until you cut the artery and reach the bone.
But you must take care to avoid the continuation of the jawbone that moves during chewing, lest the side or nerve that moves it be burned and cause spasm.
And beware of bleeding from the artery that has been cut off. For there is fear in its cutting, especially for one who does not know what he is doing and is neither studious nor experienced. He may leave the procedure before it has even begun.
And I will come with a reminder about managing blood flow from an artery according to its method and location within this book.
But if you see that the illness does not improve with this cautery and observe the patient's body unable to tolerate it in the middle of the head as we have described, then treat the wound until it heals.
And if you wish, use the cautery with two knife-like edges that we mentioned in the chapter on arterial cautery. For this cautery causes better burning and is more beneficial.
On the method of cauterizing ear pain.
When ear pain occurs due to cold and is treated with solvents and other remedies mentioned earlier but the pain does not go away, then cauterize it with fire using a cautery called 'the point,' which has this shape:
Then make dots with it around the entire ear after igniting it, as it revolves: or around both if there is pain in both ears. And lengthen the cautery from the root of the ear a little, after you have marked the places with the hot iron; and let the amount of cautery be ten punctures in every ear, and almost that.
Then treat the areas until they are healed.
About the manner of cauterizing in Torture.
Chapter VII.
The torture which is treated with cautery is only of kinds which occur from phlegm, according to what we said in the divisions of illnesses.
And avoid cauterizing species that occurs from drying out and spasm of the nerve.
When you treat this kind of torture with herbs, and purgatives, and gargarisings, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the infirm person with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and second a little lower from its time, and third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the infirm part. For softening does not occur except in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cautery is that you should cauterize with the cautery itself on the direct extremity of the upper ear under the horn of the head a little, and on the tympanum: whose length should be according to the length of the thumb. And remove your hand with the cautery until it burns through half the thickness of the skin.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a species from a cutlery knife, whose form is shown above: but it should not be too thin, as you see; and it is necessary that there be excess thickness on it a little like a knife.
Then treat the areas with what was prescribed earlier until it heals.
About the manner of cauterizing in ancient apoplexy.
When apoplexy is of long standing and the treatments we have described do not help, nor does your medication bring about any improvement, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries upon each horn of his head, and one cautery in the middle of his head as already mentioned, and another cautery at the back of his head according to what is described before: and the method of cautery should be as previously stated.
And also cauterize with a cautery upon the stomach bone, which is the last resort.
Then treat him with what preceded [i.e., the previously mentioned treatments].
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that firstly the patient be given a large dose of hyera (a medicine made from the dung of a black ox) and pills to purge the brain.
Next, shave the whole head of the patient, and place upon the back of his head the plaster made from mustard described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it frequently.
For that indeed is the method of cautery: and do this according to the same order which I have described there [i.e., earlier in the treatise].
If therefore he is cured by it, that is good. But if not, then perform three cauteries on the back part of his head, descending from the upper part of his head to the lower part of his eye; and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded [i.e., the previously mentioned treatments].
But if you wish to add more and the patient can tolerate it, then perform a cautery in the middle [of his head]. But if you wish to add still further, then cauterize him upon both horns.
Then treat him until he is cured; and let the cautery be of olive-oil according to the shape which has been prescribed.
On the method of cauterizing in the case of Paralysis and softening [of limbs].
Chapter X
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head using hyera, and with what we have said.
Next, shave the head of the patient; then cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and cauterize every horn [temple] of the head, and cauterize behind it, and three times over the nape of the neck.
If the disease requires many mollifications of the body and the patient is tolerant but the illness is strong: then cauterize him four times with a cautery over the nape of his back, and the last one until it burns deeply into his skin, and raise your hand. Then treat him until he is healed: and thus cauterize with oil.
And how to cauterize for epilepsy.
The epileptic is not cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore it is necessary that you cleanse his brain first with hyera, and with the rest of the treatment which we have mentioned in the division: when the patient is great or is tolerant to accepting medicines.
But if it is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then gargarisms and cleansing chewables should be administered to him for many days before with good food.
Then shave his head; then cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what has preceded in method: and cauterize another on his occiput, and cauterize over every horn of his head. But if the patient is strong and is tolerant then cauterize him with cauteries which I have mentioned in paralysis, and mollifications of the body over the nape of his neck and back: and let the cautery be oiled according to the method that has preceded.
But if the patient is a child then place a fine cautery, according to this method.
And how to cauterize for melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted moistures and thick phlegm then cauterize him with cauteries which we have mentioned in paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is abundance flowing towards melancholy, and the body of the sick is moistened, then give him in drink that cleanses his brain according to what has preceded in division: then shave the head of the sick, and afterwards make a turban well made of linen like a crown.
Then place it in the middle of his head: and let the sick person sitting squarely be held from every side.
Then present ointment. It is better made from old sheep butter. And warm it over a fire with moderate heat, which the finger can tolerate when inserted into it. Then pour it onto his head in a circle and let it sit until it cools.
Do this for the sick person once every week with the rest of his good regimen until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize him by making many small punctures around it, except where you hold your hand with the cautery: in fact, let there be a smell.
This kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place over it a cotton wick soaked in butter or chicken fat.
Method of cauterizing in water descending to the eye.
Chapter 13
When it is declared to you that the beginning of water is in the eye by signs which I have mentioned in division, then begin and give the sick person drink with that which cleanses his head.
And protect him from all moistures, and make him sit in a bath for several days while fasting.
Then command him to shave his head and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him over both temples with two cauteries if there is the beginning of water descending into both eyes at once, or on one side if there is the beginning of water in one eye: and cut off with a cautery all veins and arteries that are under the skin: and let the cauteries be long in breadth like the temples: and keep away from bleeding.
If you see anything from him, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and cutting them off, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck under two bones with two cauteries extended at the end.
About the way of cauterizing old tears.
When the tears of the eyes are old and continuous, and there are veins and arteries on top of them that are clearly visible on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from cold and phlegmatic excesses: then cauterize with a cautery the same as I have described for the beginning of descending water, placing one cautery in the middle of the head, two cauteries over both temples, and two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if you need additional caution, then carefully cauterize each side of the eye over the eyebrow with a small cautery.
About the way of cauterizing for foul-smelling nose.
When you treat that with what we have said about division and it does not help the treatment, then hurry and give him to drink cochlias three nights in a row: then shave his head and cauterize him with a middle-sized cautery using olive oil. Then cauterize him with a small cautery-shaped cautery on both eyebrows under the hair, a little.
And protect from the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the shape of the small cautery.
And how to cauterize for softening the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by sickness or moisture, then cauterize it with one cautery, like this crescent-shaped cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries on every part; and they will become elongated in two times [i.e., periods]; and let the length of all the cautery be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not place your hand last with the cautery, but rather according to the quantity that is burned, one-third of the eyelid.
And how to cauterize the eyelid when hairs grow inwards and prick the eye.
The cautery for this is of two kinds: either a cautery with fire, or a cautery with burning medicine.
But before applying the cautery with fire, instruct the patient to remove his hairs, if he has them for that purpose, until they grow out and become even. But if [the hairs] prick him at their origin, then compress his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they grow out.
And when they have grown out and become even, then place the head of the patient on your lap; next, mark the eyelid of his eyes with a hot iron, making the mark like the shape of a myrtle leaf; let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cotton wick soaked in egg white or marshmallow gum on the eye.
Then with fire, use this shaped cautery.
Then cauterize over the mark you made gradually in many places until the skin surface burns completely like the proper shape of a myrtle leaf.
And the sign of the cure of your operation is: if you see the eyelid of the eye now contracting and the hairs raised at the point of entry into the eye.
Therefore lift up your hand then: and let him go for three days.
Then put on him a poultice with butter until the slough is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
But if some of the hairs return after an hour and the eyelid softens: then cauterize that place again as you did at first.
If the hairs are below: then cauterize them until they rise to their natural place and become even so that they do not prick the eye.
You should instruct the patient to let their hair grow until it reaches its full length and is even. Make a pattern of the laurel leaf shape from paper.
Next, take an equal weight (uncia I) of known soap and unslaked lime, mix them thoroughly with care, so that it does not cool. Then take some of this mixture and spread it onto the paper pattern you made in the shape of a laurel leaf. Place it on the eyelid of one or both eyes. And place under the eye a cloth soaked in egg white, and have the patient's head resting in your lap.
Place your index finger on the medication and press it gently for a moment. And whenever the patient feels the medicine biting, move it gently, as its bite is like fire.
When the sensation of being bitten continues as described, then remove the medication and move it with your finger. Once the biting sensation has ceased, remove the medication and wash the eye with water.
And then observe whether the eyelid lifts up as it does when cauterized with fire or cut. If not, apply more medication to the area where it has not taken effect and darkened, until your procedure achieves the desired result and the eye contracts.
Then place a cloth soaked in butter on it until the burned skin is healed. Then treat it with diaphanous ointment or another one until it heals.
And during the procedure, you must take the utmost care to ensure that no medication falls into the eye.
But if the eyelid becomes softened after a few days and something from the hair falls into the eye, apply the medication again to that area where the eyelid has softened, as you did initially. Then treat it until it heals.
And this is the shape of the laurel leaf.
And know that human eyes differ in size and weakness. Therefore, your consideration should be this: the path of righteousness is not hidden from him who strives for excellence in this art.
On the method of cauterizing in a tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula and it does not improve with what we have said about divisions of ailments, then it is necessary to cauterize it in this manner.
Instruct the patient to place his head on your lap and have an assistant hold it between their hands so that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place a poultice soaked in albumen of egg or slippery elm mucilage over his eye. Then take the cautery whose shape is like this:
It should be hollow like the shape of a swan's feather quill from one end to the other. And if you wish it to penetrate all the way to the other end, or if you wish it to slope upwards, then test it thus.
However, this hollow shape is best for your purpose.
Then express the fistula if it is open and remove its pus and dry it out. And if it is not open then open it and remove its pus.
Then place on it the cautery which has been heated very well.
And hold it with your hand against the cautery for a short time near the eye towards the nose so that your hand does not slip or disturb the patient. Then place the cautery in the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
If you reach the beginning of your cautery up to the mouth, it will be well done. And if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice if necessary. And leave it for three days.
Then place cotton with butter and dress it with a drying ointment until it heals.
But if forty days pass and it does not heal, then apply a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed. And scrape it according to what comes up in its chapter.
And there is another method of cautery for a fistula, which some first described. Pay attention to the location of the fistula and find it. Then place in its opening a thin cannula, that is, a fine tube, which has this shape. And pour into it the amount of a dram of melted lead, and hold your hand with good retention on the tube so that the patient does not move at all, lest the molten lead reach his eye.
And it is necessary to place over the eye of the patient cotton soaked in egg white or water.
For lead burns the location of the fistula and heals it with wonderful healing.
But if the fistula heals with what we have said regarding cautery and treatment, that is good. But if not, then it is necessary to perform trephining of the nose and reduce the fistula to its course through the nose according to what will come up in its own place.
On the method of cautery for cracks in the lips.
Fissures often occur in the lip, which are called 'hairs', especially in children's lips.
But when you treat these fissures and the treatment does not help, then prepare a small cautery knife with this shape.
And its hollow should be like that of a scalpel.
Then quickly place it while hot into the actual fissures until the cautery reaches the bottom of them.
Then dress it with wax, until it heals.
On the Method of Cauterizing a Fistula on the Face.
When an abscess occurs at the root of a gum, or on the palate, or at the roots of teeth; then pus forms and bursts: afterwards it becomes hard, and pus continues to flow, and a fistula forms: if treatment is ineffective, then you must prepare a cautery according to its size that can fit into the fistula. Then insert it while hot into the opening of the fistula and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its bottom and end; do this once or twice.
Then dress it afterwards with what was mentioned about dressing until it heals.
If the pus is cut off and heals, that will be good. But if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the rotted bone according to how it comes to its head.
On the Method of Cauterizing Softened Gums and Teeth.
When the gum is softened due to moisture and the teeth are loose, and treatment with medicines does not help; then place the patient's head on your lap.
Then prepare a cautery of the shape that will be described later so that you can place a cannula over the tooth; insert the heated cautery quickly into it and hold your hand briefly until the patient feels the heat of the fire having reached the root of the tooth.
And raise your hand; then repeat the cautery as many times as you wish.
Then let the patient fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for one hour; then spit it out.
The tooth's movement is strengthened, and the gums are softened and tightened, thus drying out corrupted moisture.
On the method of cauterizing for tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to coldness, whether it's caused by cold itself or a worm, and treatment with medicines does not help: then cauterization is necessary in two ways: either using a cautery with butter or using a hot cautery.
The cautery with butter is made by taking fresh butter and melting it in an iron spoon or bronze vessel. Then take a piece of cotton, dip it into the melted butter, and apply it to the tip of the tooth. Then immerse the cotton in boiling butter, quickly apply it to the painful tooth, and hold it until it cools. Repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth.
If you wish, immerse wool or cotton in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth. Then put a hot iron on top of it until the heat reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Cauterization with fire is done using an air tube or an iron tube. And it should have some thickness to prevent the heat from reaching the patient's mouth.
Then take the cautery with fire, whose shape you will see, and apply it to that tooth. Hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times; for the pain will be removed either on the same day or on another day.
And when using that cautery, the patient should fill their mouth with good butter and hold it for one hour; then spit it out.
This is the shape of the cautery.
You can use whichever end you wish to cauterize, as much as possible. This is the shape of the tube.
On the method of cauterizing boils.
When boils are filled with phlegm and cold moistures, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, and require rapid digestion, then use a hollow cautery heated over fire, the shape of which is as follows.
It has two open ends, so that smoke can escape from one end. Place the heated cautery on the boil once or twice until it reaches the depth of the boil.
If the boil is small, then place the cautery according to its size.
Then leave it for three days and apply a poultice made with butter until what was burnt by the fire falls off.
Then treat it with toothache salve until it heals in the shape of a tube.
On the method of cauterizing for hoarseness of voice and shortness of breath.
When excess moistures accumulate on the lung canal, especially when it is accompanied by coldness of temperament, then first evacuate the patient with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it at night on the root of the throat in a depressed place, and be careful not to reach the throat itself or the skin except for a small part.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck on the last vertebra. The cautery should be shaped like a nail according to the previous method.
Then treat it with what preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing for lung ailments and coughing.
When coughing and lung ailments are caused by cold moistures, the patient does not have fever or phthisis, and the ailment is long-standing, then cauterize them with two cauteries on the fork of the neck in depressed, soft, empty places. And cauterize [them] elsewhere in the middle of the chest between the two breasts with another cautery which is like the shape mentioned before.
And if you wish to cauterize by pricking with a cautery, that is called 'Punctum', the shape of which was mentioned before in pricking ear pain, and let there be [made] thirty prickings up to nearly another.
Then treat him as mentioned before until he recovers.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this shape. Therefore the cauterization is alleviated when you use instead of one cautery three cauteries at once.
Chapter 27.
When the head of the shoulder joint is dislocated due to moistures and it does not return to its proper place within an hour after being dislocated, until that becomes a habit for him, then it should be reduced first. Then let the patient lie on his back or on his healthy side. Then lift up with your left hand's fingers the skin which is inside the armpit going upwards; and if the joint is dislocated inward.
Then take a cautery with two branches. And its shape is as follows.
Then cauterize the skin until it pierces through to the other side; and the shape of the cauterization will come out with four cauteries.
And sometimes cauterization is done with a cautery having three branches, in which case the shape of the cauterization will be six cauteries, and there are branches according to the fineness of the skin.
This is the shape of the cautery having three branches.
And sometimes one is added to this manner, therefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place over the cautery crushed garlic mixed with salt. Next, make the patient lie still so that they do not move the limb at any time until it has healed.
And if there is a dislocation towards the upper parts, which rarely occurs, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a claw-shaped cautery or by piercing with multiple cauteries.
For the union is strengthened and moisture is removed: and the patient is healed.
On the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When coldness and much moisture occur in the stomach to the point that it is removed from its proper condition, and thick mucus accumulates upon it, and frequent remedies are attempted without success, then the patient should be made to lie on their back and extend their legs and arms. Then cauterize with three cauteries: one under the curvature of the chest equal to the length of a finger with a claw-shaped cautery, and two below it on both sides of another cautery until the shape of the cauteries forms a triangle. And space them out so that they do not join together, lest they produce pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be equal to two-thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without addition: and if you wish, cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form: and let the cautery used for this cautery be one according to the shape of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking those who are tormented by this cautery: and it is as follows; that you mark upon the stomach a point according to the quantity which you wish with encaustum; then cauterize it with the cautery of the prick; then treat it with the treatment that preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver due to coldness and dampness, or from thick windiness, until it can naturally discharge its surplus through a proper exit, even though the patient has been treated with what we have already mentioned without improvement, then the patient should be made to lie on his back and three cauteries of this shape and size should be applied to the liver below the hypochondria where the elbow reaches. The space between each cautery should be the thickness of a finger, and each cautery should be as long as the length of the body itself. Do not press too hard with your hand when applying the cautery.
And let the amount burned be half the thickness of the skin, without adding more. And let the patient stand on his feet.
But if he cannot stand, then let him lie down with his legs extended and his arms raised.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And indeed it is possible for you to cauterize these points with a surgical knife when skill and prudence are present in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed too far in cauterizing, burning through the entire thickness of the skin, for then the whole body will be burned and reach the intestines. Know this.
On the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When an abscess forms and you wish to know whether it is in the flesh of the liver or its tunic: if it is in the flesh of the liver, pain occurs without sharpness but with heaviness; if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is severe acute pain. You now see that its treatment has fatigued the physicians.
Therefore, let the patient lie on his back. Then mark the location of the abscess with a branding iron; then heat the cautery which resembles a rod. This is its shape. And cauterize it with one burn until all the skin is consumed and it reaches the abscess so that all pus may discharge. Then dress it according to the method for healing discharges until it heals.
And one should not use this kind of cautery unless someone has prolonged study in the art of medicine and whose hands have often practiced such ailments with experience. Then alone may they dare to perform such operations.
But it is better for me to leave it at that.
On the method of cautery in Pleurisy.
The ancients said that for cold pleurisy, one should use a cautery with the roots of aristolochia in this manner. And one should take from dried roots of aristolochia a single root that is longer than the others, and it should be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil; and light it on fire. Then cauterize once with the cautery at the junction of the neck and collarbone, and twice with small cauteries slightly slanted towards the side that is under the beard.
And twice more with cauteries slightly slanted towards the back at the space between the fifth and sixth ribs; and once with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and once above the stomach. And three cauteries from the back: one at the space between the shoulder blades; and two cauteries on both sides of the chest, with the lower cautery being that which is between the shoulder blades.
And do not press your hand while using the cautery; rather, let it be plainly visible on the skin, with the smell indicating its location.
And some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery made of iron like a rod, and they ignite it and insert it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess itself, so that pus may discharge, as we have mentioned in the case of liver abscess.
But with this cautery method there is fear that either the patient dies immediately or a fistula forms in its place, which cannot be healed.
Chapter 32. On the Method of Cauterizing the Spleen.
When you treat an inflammation of the spleen, as we have said regarding its treatment among the divisions of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then there are three methods of cautery for it, all of which are correct.
The first method is to make three or four cauteries along the length of the spleen according to its shape, like those for the liver, whose figure has been previously described.
And let each cautery be as thick as a finger's breadth, or slightly more.
And the method of cautery should be done equally, as we have said for the cautery of the liver.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; let the patient lie on their back with their face up.
And another method of cautery is: take a cautery with two prongs, as described in the chapter on dislocations of the arm. Then lift the skin that is directly over the spleen where the left elbow reaches when the patient's arm is extended, and make your lifting just wide enough so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert the two heated prongs deeply until they penetrate through to the other side of the skin. Then remove the cautery, so that four cauteries are made in total.
And if you wish, you may cauterize with a cautery having three prongs.
Then care for the cauteries after you remove them, allowing them to discharge pus for many days; this is more beneficial than any previous treatments.
Chapter [33]. On the Method of Cauterizing in Hydropsia.
A cautery should not be applied to one suffering from hydropsy except by a skilled physician.
When you are treating a person with hydropsy using the methods of treatment that we have mentioned earlier, and the treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to cauterize [them] with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, another on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the shoulder blades, and one on the chest, and another on the stomach. The depth of the cautery should be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open so that it may discharge pus over a long period of time.
And do not remove the patient from treatment after cauterization. Rather, it is necessary for two intentions to be joined together: and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
But the form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be like a nail, according to its shape. And that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its shape.
Chapter [34]. On the Method of Cauterizing Feet and Legs.
When swellings occur in the feet of a person with hydropsy and they fill up with yellowish water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the point called 'nocrati,' which is between the heel bone (auricularem) and the ankle bone (anularis). Then lift your hand with the cautery and do not twist it. Then lift your hand again and do not repeat the process at all.
For yellowish water will dry up, and the cautery should have this shape.
Then perform two cauteries on each leg, with the cautery having the shape of a small knife at its end. Make one cautery along the length of the leg, one below the knee and another below that, about midway down the leg. Perform two cauteries on the hip joint. Leave the cautery open without further treatment for a long period of time so that some water may be absorbed from it. Then treat [the patient] with the remaining methods we have mentioned.
Concerning the method of cauterization in an abdominal incision.
Chapter 35
When the abdomen is swollen due to coldness and dampness, until it weakens the powers of retention and digestion which are in the stomach and intestines, and this condition is treated with various remedies but does not heal, you will see that the patient cannot tolerate cauterization because of excessive vigor. Then cauterize the area over the stomach using a large cautery according to what has been previously described for cauterizing the stomach with a ring cautery, and four small cauteries around the umbilicus using a fine awl cautery. Also apply a large cautery or two cauteries above the bladder.
And if you see abundant dampness and the patient cannot tolerate it, then cauterize them with a cautery over the pubic region and another over the entire hip joint. You might also add two small cauteries near the large stomach.
For this is a beneficial treatment whose aid does not fail.
Concerning the method of cauterizing hemorrhoids.
Chapter 36
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one large one, caused by thick, cold humors or corrupted dampness, and they have been treated with the method mentioned earlier for division but do not improve, then cauterize three times over the lower spine of the back just below the hip bone in a triangular pattern, and once under the umbilicus about two fingers' breadth.
And if you consider that his stomach is cold and his food is not digested, and you see his face discolored, then cauterize him over the stomach with a large cautery as previously described, another over his liver, and one over his spleen using an awl cautery. Leave the cautery open for some time, then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you divide an artery, then heat the cautery which resembles a glowing coal. Then insert the heated cautery into the divided artery until it reaches the opening of the vein from which blood flows; do this once or twice.
If there are many arteries, then cauterize each one with a cautery as we have described. Then treat them with the appropriate ointments until they heal.
And if you cauterize him with a large cautery over the stomach, it is more effective as a final remedy.
On the method of cauterizing an anal fistula.
Chapter XXXVIII.
If the patient does not respond to the incision and operation described earlier, and is afraid of it, perhaps it will heal with cautery.
When an anal fistula occurs and becomes chronic, pus flows from it and there are corrupt discharges. It is therefore necessary to probe it with a fine probe. Then determine the depth of its extent using the probe.
Then heat the cautery which resembles a glowing coal. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula until it reaches the depth at which the probe entered.
And repeat the cautery over it once or twice or three times depending on what is necessary.
And beware of burning the nerve if it is there, or a large vein, or if the fistula extends to the bladder or the intestines; then beware of all these areas.
And do not perform this procedure unless the fistula is located in a fleshy area and you are certain that it does not penetrate deeply.
Then dress the wound until it heals.
But if the site is sealed and no more material is being excreted from it even after a long period of time, then know that it has healed completely.
And if material continues to be excreted from it, then know that the fistula is penetrating deeply or there is a rotting bone at its base, or something similar.
Method of Cauterizing Kidneys
When pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or excess wind, and this condition weakens sexual function, then it is necessary to cauterize the area using a cautery spoon placed over the kidneys. Cauterize each kidney with an iron cautery and a claw-shaped cautery.
And perhaps we cauterize again on the following day. So there will be three cautery marks. Therefore, they will be most helpful for healing.
Method of Cauterizing the Bladder
When weakness and laxity occur in the bladder due to cold and humidity, causing the patient not to retain urine, then cauterize the lower part of the pubic area over the bladder where the pubic hair begins. Use a cautery from the right side of the pubis and another from the left; let their length be equal to the breadth of the thumb. Also cauterize the lower back of the bladder with a single or double cautery, according to what is needed.
Method of Cauterizing the Uterus
When cold and humidity affect the uterus causing infertility, disrupting menstruation, delaying ovulation, and resulting in pain during menstruation, then it is necessary to cauterize three times around the navel using cauteries of the same length as those used for cauterizing the bladder. Also cauterize below the back of the ribs with a single or double cautery.
On the method of cauterization for the anus in cases of dislocation.
When mucous discharges reach the anus and cause its prolapse from its proper place, with one leg extended over the other as a sign, and the location of the prolapse is found to be empty.
It is necessary to cauterize the inflamed area around the anus with a cautery of circular shape. After marking with a hot iron around the circumference of the prolapsed tissue, ensure that the tissue falls into the center of the circle.
But if you do not have this cautery present, then cauterize with three cauteries using a large olive-shaped cautery, making the depth of the cautery according to the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it until it heals.
On the method of cauterization for sciatica.
When pain occurs in the anus and is caused by coldness and humidity, and treatment using diuretics does not help, then it is necessary to remove the thick humors with foul-smelling pills or similar artificial pills. Then cauterize him.
The method of cauterization in this case is done in two ways: either with a cautery using burning medicines, or with a cautery heated with fire.
A cautery with fire has many methods.
One method is to cauterize the anus itself three times using triangular cauteries in this shape: ∆. And make it either a good or bad depth. And let the space between each cautery be as thick as a finger. And let the cauteries be oiled.
Sometimes, however, a cautery is applied directly onto the head of the anus itself. So there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circular cautery, the form of which is as follows for the cautery of anal prolapse, use one that completely encircles the anus.
Burn through the entire thickness of the skin.
This is the method of cautery for sciatica when pain adheres to the anus itself and does not extend up to the hip and thigh.
But if it extends up to the hip and thigh, then cauterize it with two cauteries on the hip at the location where the sick person indicates that pain is felt. And also cauterize along the groove of the buttocks about four fingers from the genital region using a knife-shaped cautery.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the thickness of the skin.
If the sick person indicates that pain extends nearly to the toes, then cauterize there where they indicate using a puncturing cautery, three or four times, or more if necessary.
And if they indicate that pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then cauterize there using one knife-shaped cautery.
But be careful in all your cauteries so that you do not burn through to the nerves or a large artery and thereby cause harm or contraction to the sick person.
And indeed I have seen one person and another among those who cauterized along the buttocks and burned through too deeply, causing swelling of the thigh that spread to the foot until it became completely perforated and corrupted. Then gangrene set in, followed by death.
If pain is felt in two parts at once, cauterize both according to this method.
And certain wise men have spoken concerning the cautery of the ankle, which is the subject of this method. Make a mold like this one out of iron, whose diameter is half the length of a palm; and let it have at its opening the thickness of a finger joint or less; and inside that mold there should be another mold.
And let the space between each mold be equal to the thickness of a thumb joint; and let the molds be open at both ends, with a height of about one or two joints; and make them a well-fitted handle out of iron.
Then heat it in a fire until it glows red and sparks fly off; then place it on the ankle bone of the sick person lying on their healthy side. So cauterize him with three round cauteries in place of one.
Then leave him for three days. Afterward, apply poultices with butter; and allow the wound to remain open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, 'We have rarely used this kind of cautery, because of its frightening appearance and because we found few people who would endure it.'
Nevertheless, it is one of the good cauteries for those who can bear it, and it finds its proper place.
But the cautery with burning medicines is like this: make two molds having a pierced ring into which descends the pin of its door made of iron or bronze, equal to their height.
And let the space between them be equal to the thickness of a finger joint, and let them be open at the bottom and top; and let them fit together like this.
Then place it on a board of lead, with the sick person lying on their healthy side. And press your hand firmly upon the board of lead. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been heated with fire for a short time, and hold it for about an hour: and let the sick person bear its biting and scorching, for he found that the biting is like fire until the burning ceases.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and remove the hot water from the lead board entirely with fresh water; then leave it for three days.
And place upon it butter until the blackness of the burning is removed: and leave it for some days, and pus will flow from it. For this is the final remedy.
And then treat it with ointments until it heals.
But if the pain extends to the hip or thigh, make for him another such apparatus containing water, just as you did for the lead board.
And this is the method of hot water: and I have already written about it in my treatise on the correction of medicines. Take quicklime and undried slaked lime each in equal portion: grind both of them and place them in a new pot whose bottom has one small hole according to the size that the sun can enter: and place underneath the pot another pot glazed: and pour upon the quicklime and slaked lime from sweet water, so that both are submerged by one finger's breadth: then press them with your hand with good pressure: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends through the lower part of the glazed pot.
Then gather all that water and pour it upon more slaked lime and grind until it renews itself.
This will then be of very strong sharpness, which is used in many operations in medicine and in the cautery of other limbs. Because it makes the action of fire itself effective.
And among the medicines are those with which ulcers are cauterized, such as tessia and manna, and chalk mixed with soap, so that each may be well combined.
And indeed Galen has reported the story of a man from ancient times who was cured of the pain of ulcers and sciatic veins by this treatment, which he greatly praised. And he said that he did not require any other treatment and that he was cured with just one application; until he reported that perhaps he entered the bath carried and came out of it already healed.
And it should be taken from green sittairga; and if the green is not found, fresh dried may be taken and ground much with some fat and placed upon the ulcer or leg or thigh where there is pain, and bound on, and allowed to remain for a period of three hours or until the patient feels relieved from the burning sensation. Then immerse him in a bath.
When his body becomes moist, then put him on a seat. For the pain subsides and the wound is healed.
And know that one should not use a cautery with these medicines unless after evacuating the body.
And Dioscorides also said that goat droppings, when used with it to cauterize the sciatic vein, are beneficial for this purpose, and a cautery is made according to this method. Take wool and impregnate it with old oil and place it upon the deep hollow which is between the big toe of the foot and the heel, closer to the heel.
Then take dry goat droppings and burn them in fire until they become charcoal.
Then place it upon the wool and let it remain until it is extinguished. Then repeat this process. Do not cease doing this until sensation reaches the ulcer and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the vaccinating cautery.
On the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain occurs in the back due to many causes, either by chance, or from impact, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and humid matter: and cautery is not applied except in this single type, which occurs from the infusion of cold matter.
It is therefore necessary, after evacuating the sick person with fetid pills and similar things, so that they are placed on the back where the pain is located, to draw three lines according to its width. Then, mark with a hot iron in every line five cauterizations, or more according to the quantity which comes from the tolerance of the sick person's strength. And let the cauterization be done with a cautery point.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using the middle nail cautery, according to this shape.
On the method of cauterizing at the beginning of a hump.
This illness often occurs in young infants.
And the sign of its beginning in children is: that tightness occurs upon him during elevation and movement, and you will find at the last spine of the back and its nodes, that it has already begun to rise above the remaining spines.
When therefore you see this, and wish to do this, then cauterize it with a cautery that is circular according to this shape.
And let the cautery cover the entire part of the spines evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spines with a point cautery two or three lines, and let the points be close together.
Then treat the place until it heals with what we have said.
And take care not to administer a cautery on a hump which occurs due to nerve spasm.
On the method of cauterizing for gout and joint pains.
When joint pains are caused by cold moistures which flow to any part of the body, then when these pains occur in the feet, it is customary among physicians to name this 'Podagra' properly.
Therefore, when gout caused by coldness is being treated with various methods of treatment and the pains are not removed, then cautery removes them.
And it is necessary to cauterize him after evacuation around the joint of the feet with many cauteries; and let the cautery be olive oil.
If you wish to make punctures on the surface of the foot, then do so with a cautery. But if the pains ascend to the knees or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize the entire knee with three cauteries, or four on all sides, with the same cautery of Claudianus.
If however you need more of this cautery, then cauterize it [the foot]. And do not immerse your hand with the cautery, but let it be about as thick as the skin.
But if the pains ascend to the knees and back: then apply what we have said from the cautery according to its chapter.
What if the pains are only in the hands? Then make punctures around the joints like two lines revolving.
But if there remain any pains in the fingers, then puncture them on every joint and on the palm of the hand.
But if the pains ascend after some days to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize both on all sides.
And do not evacuate the patient from a good regimen, nor from receiving medicines. For if a good regimen is established and phlegm is evacuated, the illness will be cured with God's help along with this cautery.
On the method of cauterizing ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groin and an intestine or spermatic cord descends, and it is beginning to be close by: then you should order the patient to refrain from food on that day. And let him use gentle laxatives so that feces may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands upon his back: and command him to hold his breath until it passes out, or the spermatic cord or intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers and mark [the spot] with a cautery beneath the rupture above the pubic bone, with a sign whose upper end is like half of a circle.
Then heat the cautery which has this shape until it becomes white-hot and emits sparks. Then reduce the intestine or spermatic cord to its hollow. Then let the assistant place his hand on the spot so that the intestine does not slip out: and you have now opened between the patient's thighs, placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant is upon his legs, and another upon his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery upon the mark itself with your hand holding it upright. And hold it until you reach the bone with it; or repeat [the process] once more if you did not reach the bone on the first attempt.
And carefully observe that no intestine escapes during your cautery operation, lest you burn it and cause harm or serious injury to the patient.
And know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your operation is useless.
And it is necessary for children to have a fine cautery according to their size.
Then care for [the patient] with the remaining ointments until he is healed.
And let the patient lie upon his back for forty days until the wound closes.
And it is necessary that you provide nourishment suited to the duration of his treatment, which will soothe his stomach: so that no part of his intestines may be affected during excretion and digestion.
Then, when he wants to rise after forty days, then apply a well-made bandage, and let it stay for another forty days.
And reduce his labor, food intake, and drink, and prevent violent coughing.
For when he follows this regimen, he will be cured completely.
And I shall speak of the treatment of Ruptures with Incision in its own chapter.
But when ruptures occur in the remainder of the abdomen and are beginning, and you wish that they not increase, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size; and let that which is burned be like a third of it. Then treat it as we have said, and it will not increase.
And some of the first ones said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, in this shape.
After it is marked with the cautery, and a line is placed that goes across the width on the upper side of the rupture, and another line below. And place your hand in the middle with the keyhole-shaped cautery.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Regarding the method of cauterization for pains caused by a fall or blow.
Chapter 48.
When pain occurs in some limbs due to a fall or blow and persists for a long time without improvement despite treatment with medicines, then it is necessary to cauterize it with the puncturing cautery.
And let the cautery for each member be according to its size, thickness, weakness, strength, location of the twist, and pain caused by it.
If it is cured after the first cauterization, that is good. But if not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
For it is customary with these pains that they shift from one member to that which is near it. Therefore you should pursue them with a cautery until the patient is healed.
On the manner of cauterizing in Leprosy.
But sometimes lepers are greatly benefited by cautery. And especially that type of leprosy which arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. Therefore, when you wish to cauterize it, consider.
But if leprosy is beginning and you have treated it with what we said in the division, and it does not subside nor stop, and you fear that corruption will spread over the whole complexion of the patient, then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, and a second below it towards the forehead at the end of the hair, and two on the two horns [of the forehead], and one behind on the nape of the neck.
And lastly apply your hand with the cautery lightly until it makes a small impression on the bone, and the skin layers are loosened from it; so that the expiration of thick vapors from it may be alleviated, and cauterize also the spleen according to what preceded.
But if leprosy has already spread over the patient and appears manifestly, then you must cauterize with those cauteries which we said for the head, and one on the tip of the nose, and two on both jaws, and two on both collarbones, and six on the ribs of the back, and one large one at the buttocks near to the tailbone and one above it in its depth: and two on the hips, that is on all the hip one, and two on both knees: one on all knee joints, and two on shoulders, and two on elbows, and two on the softnesses of his chest: and cauterize him on all jointures from the jointures of his fingers hands and feet; and cauterize also over all heel of his feet and palm of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are upon the heel lest thou burn them.
Also, cauterize with a cautery on the breastbone, and another on the stomach bone, and another on the liver.
And know that the more you prolong the cautery, the greater is the benefit and advantage.
And know that the patient does not find pain in cauterization as the healthy do; because his body is already numbed.
And it is necessary that the cauteries be of such size and fineness according to the members and joints as we have previously described concerning the kinds of instruments.
Then care for the cauteries with herb flour mixed with honey, and other remedies until it heals.
On the manner of cauterizing in Stupor.
When some member becomes paralyzed and is treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and yet does not recover, then cauterize the paralyzed member with cauteries according to its size or smallness.
And let your cautery penetrate slightly into the thickness of the skin for a brief moment. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
And sometimes cauterization is applied to a certain numbness that occurs in the hand and foot, at the hip bones of the back near the exit of the nerves which move those limbs; and the numbness is removed.
But let no one presume to do this except someone who is wise in anatomy of the limbs and the exit of moving nerves.
Chapter 51
When the Albaras is cauterized and nothing can be accomplished with medical techniques, then cauterize it with a deep cautery briefly, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its color changes.
Then treat it with flour of barley, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of sage, and dove's blood, and thrush's blood: let each be one part; mix all these together and apply them on a bandage, and let them adhere to the place until it heals.
About the method of cauterizing in Cancer.
When a cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it: then cauterize its circumference with a circular cautery all around it, as it revolves.
But wise men have said that it should be cauterized with the last point of the cautery in the middle.
But I do not think this, for I fear that it may ulcerate; and I have already seen this happen many times.
And it is better to cauterize its circumference with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
About the method of cauterizing in Adubelati (Hernia).
When someone has a hernia that is delayed in its reduction, either because of excess fluid causing it or because of the advanced age of the patient who is weak and has little blood, or because of the time it has been present, and you wish to hasten the reduction of the hernia, then cauterize around its circumference with many small cauteries, puncturing. Then leave it alone. For it will reduce on its own.
But if you wish to perform a puncture of the hernia with a cautery, then heat the cautery which has this shape.
And place it in the middle of the hernia until it pierces the skin, and let the cautery be slightly inferior to where it follows, so that the course of the purified fluid may be alleviated.
Then treat it until it heals.
And regarding the method of cauterizing a malignant ulcer.
Chapter 52
A corrupting ulcer is nothing but corruption that travels along a limb and consumes it, like fire devouring dry wood.
If therefore you see a corrupting ulcer in a place that can withstand being cauterized with fire, then heat many cauteries, some small and some large, according to what is fitting for the spot where the corruption is.
Then cauterize it on all sides until you have erased the entire corruption, so that nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it alone for three days, and place powdered sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized areas until all scabs and corruption are removed.
Then treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is generated without corruption, then it is good.
But if not, then repeat the cautery on whatever remains of the corrupted areas.
And sometimes a corrupting ulcer is treated with an acrid medication. For it itself arises from the place of the cautery.
However, cauterization with fire is a quicker remedy. And indeed I have already mentioned cauterization of it with an acrid medication in the section on division: therefore take that there when you need it.
On the manner of cauterizing fingernails and warts.
Chapter 56.
It often happens that this illness occurs in the lower parts of the feet, and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And indeed cauterization in these [cases] is according to two methods: cauterization with fire and cauterization with hot water.
The amount of cautery with fire should be like a hollow cautery resembling the feather of an eagle made from iron, according to the quantity that contains the nail on all sides and has sharp edges.
Then place the heated cautery upon the nail. Then revolve the hand with the cautery around the nail until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail, and leave it there for three days until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply a poultice with wild mallows crushed with salt upon it, and leave the poultice over it during the night. For it will be eradicated from its roots.
Then care for the place with an ointment that generates flesh until it heals.
But if they are not converted and often occur on the surface of the body, particularly in hands and feet, then you should administer cauterization with hot water. And this is done by taking a cannula made from bronze or iron or eagle's feather and placing it upon the nail or callus. Then pour a small quantity of hot water into the cannula and keep your hand steady as you rotate it with gentle pressure so that the edge of the cannula impresses upon the root of the nail, allowing the hot water to find its way to the depth. And let the patient wait for about an hour until the burning sensation from the hot water has subsided.
Then leave him alone, for the nail will be removed along with its roots.
Do this one at a time until you have done them all in the body.
Then care for them after they are removed with ointments that generate flesh.
On the method of cauterizing a tremor.
When trembling occurs in someone due to coldness of the nerve, or from quartan fever, or from some other cause: then it is necessary to cauterize them with four cauteries, or five, on the spine of the back, and between every spine with a cautery, and one on the chest, and another on the stomach.
For trembling ceases when cauterized with an oil cautery, and health hastens the recovery of the frozen illness.
On the method of cauterizing 'albatheer' (a type of tumor).
Chapter 67.
Sometimes foul tumors called 'albathir' are expelled from the body, that is, pustules caused by corrupted materials.
Therefore, when they first appear, it is necessary to cauterize them with a fine cautery made of myrtle wood, the tip of which has been set on fire. 'Or with the root of long aristolochia.' Or with a lens-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized bit by bit at the beginning of their eruption according to this method, and they do not increase; and the excess that causes them is broken up, and they are healed.
But it should be done after evacuation with bloodletting.
On the method of cauterizing bleeding from an artery wound.
Often it happens that blood flows from an artery which has been cut during a wound made externally, or during the incision of an abscess, or cautery on a limb, and similar cases: and it is difficult to stop it.
But when such a thing happens to someone, then promptly place your hand over the artery's opening and put your index finger on it: and press it tightly until the blood is blocked under your finger and nothing flows out of it.
Then put a small olive-oil cautery into the fire, and many others likewise: and blow on them until they become very heated.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is disrupted, and put the cautery on it. Then quickly remove your finger, and hold the cautery until the bleeding stops.
But if blood is expelled when you lift your finger from the artery's opening, then quickly take another cautery that has been prepared in the fire.
Do not cease doing this with one after another until the bleeding stops.
And be careful not to burn the nerve that is there, lest another mischief happen upon the sick person.
And know that when blood flows from an artery, it is not possible to stop it except by one of four methods. Or with a cautery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is extracted, the ends of it contract and the blood stops flowing. Or it can be tied with a strong liga Or put on it medicines that have the property of stopping blood, and tie it with an appropriate compress.
But whoever tries to stop it by tying it with a bandage and compression with cloth, or with the application of burning substances and similar things, rarely succeeds.
But if this happens to someone and there is no physician present nor any medicine: then he should begin by placing his index finger over the vein's opening, as we have described, and compressing it very tightly until blood flow from above the wound is blocked off. And the finger should not be moved, while continuously applying cold water of intense coldness from above it until the blood congeals, thickens and is cut off.
And meanwhile he should consider what is needed in terms of a cautery or medicine.
On Cutting, Piercing, and Bloodletting in Wounds, and Similar Conditions.
